Carter acts secretly on rights 

WASHINGTON (A P ) - P r e s i d e n t 
Carter’s chief spokesman said Monday the adm in istra tio n has ta ken secret actions in support of human rights and will continue its public an d priv a te support despite Kremlin protests. 
Presid ential P re s s S ecre ta ry Jody 
Powell said this support should riot be linked in any way with efforts to limit strategic a rm s and noted that p re p a r­ ations for S e c r e ta r y of State C y ru s 
Vance’s trip to Moscow on M arch 28 are pr eceeding without delay. 

Warning 

Powell responded to a warning Sun­ day in the Communist part newspaper 
Pravda that Carter’s outspokenness on h u m a n rig h ts could d a m a g e th e a t ­ m o s p h e r e s u r r o u n d i n g an y f u t u r e strategic a r m s limitation talks. 
“ Detente and the normal conduct of 

 talks presuppose the establishment of trust l>etween the negotiating parties and respect for the laws and traditions of each o t h e r , " P r a v d a s a i d . “ A t­ tempts to exert pressure on us and to bargain for concessions of principles are bringing about an atm osphere of distrust.” 

The article was the latest in a series of Kremlin protests against C a r t e r ’s support for Soviet dissidents and his statements on behalf of hum an rights around the world. 

Can’t discuss 

Asked w h e t h e r C a r t e r h a s m a d e public all of his human rights activi­ ties, Powell said. “ There have been, certainly, noti-publicized activities in this regard but I ca n ’t discuss them ” 
He added, “ It ought to be noted that 

 preparations are going forward w ith­ out any delay for the V a n c e trip to 
M o sc o w .” V an c e told a m o r n i n g 
Cabinet meeting that he would m eet with Carter this week to receive final instructions for the mission. A key part jjf the trip will be discussing p re p a ra­ tions for new strategic a r m s talks. 
Powell said the administration does not link human righs or support for 
Russian dissidents with the strategic arm s talks. 

Crucial 

“ Discussions with r e g a r d to s t r a ­ tegic arm s are so crucial to tin' secur­ ity of the United States and the Soviet 
Union, and to the long-term best in­ terests of the entire world, that they can and should proceed without any linkage to any other ar e a of d i s c u s ­ sion,” Powell said. 

Asked whether Carter is concerned that the Soviets a r e linking h u m a n rights and strategic a r m s , the press secretary replied: ‘i ' m not going to try to comment on individual articles that appear from time to tim e .” 
Is there any indication th rough d i ­ plomatic channels that the Soviets an* making this link? 
“ I know of none,' Powell replied 

Clear 

“ I th i n k o u r p o s it io n on h u m a n 1 rights is clear, and we will continue, as we said at the outset, to act according to our best .judgment in support of this end,” he said. 

“ Where some public dem o n stratio n of support is best, we will so act 
Where private efforts are best we will pursue that co u rse.” 
Strauss vows to get U.S. fair deal 

N EW YO ® * t i m e s SERVICE 
WASHINGTON - Robert S Strauss, recently n am ed P re s id e n t C a r t e r ’s special trade representative, said in an interview Monday that th e United 
States had gotten short, shrift in agriculture in previous m ultilateral trade negotiations. 
He served notice that in the current round “ we're not going to give an yth­ ing aw ay.” 
He also said “ it is highly unlikely if not impossible" for the United Stall's to conclude the new round by the end of this year — a deadline that had been previously set by the major trading cowers. 

Catching up 

We have a long way to go. a lot of latching up to do.” hi' said in his law office here. 
“ We have to see where we are with our fragile economy, what luxuries we can afford. The hand will have to be played out a little longer.” 
S t r a u s s , a T e x a n who h a d bee n chairm an of the Democratic National 
Committee before accepting the trade post, is a well-known Washington poli­ tical figure with many friends in Con­ gress. hut lie has no record on inter-* national trade questions 
“ It s tough .lob — I'm not even sure it s a do uble job," he said, describing himself as “ basically a free tr a d e r. ” 
But he added, “ free trade has to he 
. luned very ca refully with econom ic reality and lobs and a healthy econ­ omy. because if w e’re going to have u n e m p l o y m e n t an d i n f l a t i o n , we simply won t be free to trade ” 
In ail hour-long conversation in the 
W a s h i n g t o n office of A kin . G u m p . 
Strauss. Hailer & Feld, his law firm. he took a relatively hard line on the c u r r e n t n eg o tiatio n s, in sistin g that other countries would have to lie fair with the United States it they wanted the round to conclude successfully 

Hallway 

“ II we're not met hallway, we won’t make a deal. “ 

He w a s c r i t i c a l of t h e K e n n e d y 
Round, the last big trade negotiations in the in id-I Mitts, for not getting e n ­ ough a d v a n t a g e s for 
A m e r i c a n farm ers and stressed that agriculture will “ certainly Im* iii the forefront" iii the current Geneva round. 

Ills c o m m e n t s p r e s a g e a s tr u g g le with the European Common Market. whose farm ers want to preserve their own agricultural markets 

French and other European t a n n e r s have long complained about shrinking living standards, com plaints that are e c h o e d bv f a r m e r s in t h e U n ite d states 

Austrian chancellor says rights concern is very im pressive 

N EW VORK TIMES SERVICE 
WASHINGTON - Chancellor Bruno 
Kreisky of Austria said Monday that he found the Carter adm inistration’s e m ­ phasis on human rights issues “ very im pressive ." But he expressed con­ cern that the campaign might dam age quieter forms of helping individuals in authoritarian societies 
Kreisky conferred Monday with Se­ cretary of State Cyrus H 
Vance and with Zbigniew Brezezinski. the P re si­ d e n t ’s national secu rity adviser. He also m e t briefly with Carter. 
Concerning dissidents in the Soviet bloc, he o b s e rv e d in an in te rv iew :

M exico oil help urged 

SPECIAL TO THE EXPRESS 
WASHINGTON - The United States should assist Mexico in. developing energy reserves in return for long­ term energy supplies at reasonable prices, said U.S. Rep. Bob Krueger 
Monday. 
Krueger’s comment came during a speech before the National Ocean In­ dustries Assn. 
“ We should look to our neighbor south of the border and w ork out arrangements exchanging technologi­ cal expertise necessary to develop th e ir energy reserves for assured long-term energy supplies at reasona­ ble prices.” Krueger said. 
Krueger said the U.S. must “ develop the technology to escape from energy blackm ail, even if we do not achieve total energy independence.” _________

Health center faces job bias charge 

Federal officials have charged the University of 
Texas Health Science ( enter here with job discri­ mination because- of age. 
U.S. Secretary of Labor Ray Marshall has asked a San Antonio federal court to compel UTHSU to hire, reinstate or promote people who wore victim s of the discrim ination. 
Federal law prohibits discrim ination i i i employ­ ment because of age against anyone between 4o and 
Im years old. 
The lawsuit states the Labor Department sought to get voluntary, compliance from UTHSU to end the d iscrim in a to r practices. 
The suit also a s k s fur payment of back pay or overtime due the victim s of alleged discrim ination. 
Marshall cann- to tin- Labor Department from the 
Austin campus of the University of Texas. 
The suit was filed by the Dallas legal office of the department. 
The UT Health Science Center includes the medi­ cal school, dental school and nursing school in the 
South Texas Medical Center.

Q uick license update urged 

The State Department of Highways and Public Transportation urges Tex­ ans to get license plate stickers now before the long lines at tin- end of 
March. 
“ May we suggest if you are among the several m illions of Texans that have not yet obtained your 1977 rod validation sticker for your rear license plate, that you take your three-part registration renewal form to the most convenient sub-station of your County 
Tax Assessor-Colleetor s office today.” a departm ent spokesman said. 
The spokesman said reports from around the state indicate many m otor­ ists have not obtained their stickers. 
The department spokesman said he fears another rush such as last year's may occur unless motorists get the stickers now

. . first trip back 

Citizen Ford plans D.C. visit 

ASSOCIATED PRISS 

WASHINGTON — Private citizen 
Gerald R. Ford and his wife plan to visit Washington March 24-26, their first trip to the nation's capital since Ford turned over the White 
House to President tarter on Jan. 
2ft. 

The Fords will spend their two nights in Washington in the official former President’s residence, a townhouse across Lafayette Park from the White House where they lived for 2*2 years. 

Ford’s press aide. Larry Speakes. 

 said Ford will attend a series of meetings at the American Enter­ prise Institute, a Republican-or­ iented economic think-tank where he is a “distinguished fellow.” 

Speakes said in a statement that 
Ford also will have a breakfast meeting with the Republican con­ gressional leadership and host a reception for several former Ca­ binet and senior staff members from his administration. 

Ford’s visit to Washington will follow three days of meetings in 
New York City with officials of the 
Fisenhower Fellowships.

Bealls opened Monday in Central Park 

Bealls newest and most modern department store staged its grand opening Monday at IO a.m. in Central 
Park Mall. 

This is Bealls third San Antonio store, joining those already established in South Park Mall and Windsor Park 
Mall. Tom Rodcs. former manager in 
South Park, will manage the new store. 
Rodes, a 21-year merchandising ve­ teran, started with Bealls in Austin in 
1973. In July 1974, he was promoted to manager at South Park. Prior to join­ ing Bealls, he was with a national chain for 17 years, including nine as manager. 
Born in Shreveport, La., he gra­ duated from high school in Benton. 
La., and received a bachelor of science degree from Shreveport’s Centenary 
College. 
He and his wife, the former Evelyn 
„ 
R „ 
Robertson of Madill, Okla., have three children. Tommy, 22, Martha. 18, and ompanv presidtnt 
Beth. 8. Thev reside at 129 Trillium, 
Bealls newest in Central Park is a family department store featuring 
Local Bealls join debut festivities 

Beads stores in South Park Mall and 
Windsor Park Mall are participating in the grand opening festivities of the 
Central Park unit. 
According to managers Charles 
Koonse at South Park and Darcey 
Ambrose at Windsor Park, both stores will have available all advertised 

 name brands and seasonal special buys in every department. 
Major departments include ladies ready-to-wear, juniors, infants, girls, cosmetics, accessories, costume jewelry, home furnishing, lingerie- sleepwear, foundations, family shoes, men s, college men and boys’. 
Tho store, located on the upper level toward the mall’s east end. is 28,ooo square feet. Accessibility to the store is through the mall or the parking lot entrance facing Loop 41o. 
Fixtures and decor are by Store 
Kraft Manufacturing Co. of Beatrice, 
Nebr., one of the leading store de­ signers in the nation. Related depart­ ments such as ladies and children’s wear are closely coordinated for shop­ ping convenience and ease. 

Contemporary look 

A fresh contemporary look prevails with an abundant use of chrome fix- turing throughout. All merchandise racks and counters display fashions at eye level for easy selection. 
An open look is evident, yet a “ bou­ tique” look is utilized in some areas, such as the junior shop and men’s departments. 
Stage type show windows, w ide spa­ cious aisles, soft background music and carpeting will greet customers entering the store. 
A spacious cosmetics department is the focal point at the mall entrance. 
Immediately adjacent is the acces­ sories department, including scarves, sunglasses, watches and small leather goods. 
To the left are the ladies and junior departments, joined by girls and In­ fants wear toward the rear of the store. 
The men’s and college men’s de­ partments are to the right of the entrance, sporting masculine decpr and furnishings. 
What may customers expect from the new Bealls? 

 specials, just as the new* store will. 
Beall officials pointed out the open­ ing is a coordinated effort so customers may enjoy sale values at the Bealls nearest them. 
Bealls in South Park was opened in 
May 1974 while the Windsor Park store 
Tom Rodes opened its doors latst July.

According to manager Tom Bodes, friendly service from sales people and quality merchandise at reasonable prices are the twin priorities. 
The store is employing area people in striving to maintain a hometown atmosphere, he added. Customer sa­ tisfaction on every purchase is a must. 
“ We just don’t want any unhappy customers," he said. Bealls still be­ lieves in waiting on people and being of help when a customer requests it. he said.
